GEOTECHNICAL ENGINEERING OBSERVATIONS SERVICES 
SOIL NAIL INSTALLATION AND TESTING 
HANA HIGHWAY ROCKFALL MITIGATION AT MILE POST 12 
HANA, MAUI, HAWAII 
Dear Mr. Tillotson: 
This letter report summarizes our geotechnical engineering observation services 
performed during the soil nail installation and testing for the Hana Highway Rockfall 
Mitigation at Mile Post 12 project, located in Hana on the Island of Maui, Hawaii. The project 
location and general vicinity are shown on the Project Location Map, Plate 1. 
In general, this letter report presents our observations and the results of the soil nail 
installation and testing performed for the project between April 21, 2021 and May 16, 2022. 
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
Hana Highway (Route 36) (from Huelo to Hana) is a winding, narrow, two-lane 
undivided road with very steep cut slopes on one side and steep natural slopes on the 
downhill side. The area is heavily vegetated due to the high rainfall experience. Additionally, 
the road is heavily used by residents and tourists. The general extent of the project limits is 
shown on the Overall Site Plan, Plate 2. 
Multiple sections of the highway in the vicinity of Mile Post 12 experienced lateral 
movements, resulting in settlement and longitudinal cracks of the highway pavements. In 
addition, several locations above the roadway experienced -localized slope failures. Soil nail 
anchors were designed and specified to mitigate the above-mentioned distress and/or 
failure as improvements of the highway. 
It was desired to provide geotechnical engineering quality control services during the 
soil nail retaining wall construction. The purpose of our geotechnical engineering services 
was to observe the installation and testing of the soil nails for general conformance with the 
project plans and specifications. 
Prometheus Construction

W.O. 8223-00 (Soil Nail Installation and Testing Report)

MAUKA UPSLOPE SOIL NAIL INSTALLATION AND TESTING 
As a part of the project requirements, an anchored wire mesh system consisting of 
individual reinforcing bars grouted into drilled holes to secure the wire mesh was designed 
to stabilize the existing slope at three different sites along Hana Highway Milepost 12. The 
approximate locations of the three sites are shown on the Overall Site Plan, Plate 2.0 and 
Site Plans, Plates 2.1 through 2.3. Approximate locations of the installed drilled anchors 
along the specified mauka upslopes are illustrated on the Mauka Anchor Layout Plans, 
Plates 3.1 through 3.3. 
A Geolabs representative observed the drilling and grouting operations during the 
installation of the soil/rock anchors. The anchors were drilled using various 
excavator-mounted drill rigs, a winch drill rig, and a boom lift-mounted drill rig. Each drill rig 
was equipped with a down-the-hole hammer with a 3.5-inch to 4-inch button hammer bit. 
After the drilled holes were extended to the specified depths, soil cuttings were 
removed from the boreholes using pressurized air. A threaded galvanized hollow reinforcing 
bar with centralizers was then inserted into the hole. A hot-dipped galvanized wire rope was 
used for the cable anchors. In general, the centralizers were placed at about 10-foot 
intervals. 
The grout was batched on-site utilizing a colloidal high-shear and high-speed 
ChemGrout CG-680 mixer equipped with a grout pump. Grouting began progressively from 
the bottom to the top through the grouting tube until fresh grout appeared at the top of the 
hole. Results of the soil nail installation records are summarized in the Summary of the 
Mauka Soil Nail Installation and Testing, Plates 5.1 through 7.5.  
In accordance with the project documents, proof tests were selected and performed 
on 20 percent of the total anchors installed, excluding the top anchors as noted from RFI 015 
dated May 14, 2021. In general, the proof test anchors were tested to about 200 percent of 
the design pull-out capacity or a maximum test load of about 44 kips for the slope face 
anchors and a maximum test load of about 36 kips for the bottom anchors.  
The following table summarizes soil nail anchors installed and tested along the 
mauka upslope at Sites 1 through 3. Details of proof testing conducted on the selected soil 
nail anchors at Sites 1 through Site 3 are presented in the attached Appendix.

MAKAI DOWNSLOPE SOIL NAIL INSTALLATION AND TESTING 
A reinforced shotcrete wall with a soil nail system was installed at the makai 
downslope area along Site 1, as shown on Plate 2.1. The approximate locations of the soil 
nails installed are shown on the Makai Wall Layout Plan, Plate 4. A total of 38 soil nails 
(15 vertical and 23 horizontal anchors) were installed at the downslope of Site 1. 
A Geolabs representative observed the drilling and grouting operations during the 
construction of the soil/rock anchors. The anchors were drilled using an excavator-mounted 
drill rig and a winch drill rig equipped with a down-the-hole hammer and a 3.5-inch to 4-inch 
button hammer bit.  
After the drilled holes were extended to the specified depth, soil/rock cuttings were 
removed from the boreholes using pressurized air.  A threaded hot-dipped galvanized bar 
(GR150 ksi) with prefabricated HDPE sheathing was inserted in the drilled hole. Centralizers 
were placed along the bar at about 10-foot intervals.  
The grout was batched on-site utilizing a colloidal high-shear and high-speed 
ChemGrout CG-680 mixer equipped with a grout pump. A 1½-inch diameter high-density 
plastic grouting tube was inserted into the drilled hole along the anchor tendon. Grouting 
began progressively from the bottom to the top through the grouting tube until fresh grout 
appeared at the top of the hole. Results of the soil nail installation records are summarized 
in the Summary of the Makai Soil Nail Installation and Testing, Plate 8. 
A total of five soil nails (two vertical and three horizontal anchors) were selected and 
proof tested, including Soil Nails V1, V10, A5, B2, and C6. The proof test soil nails were 
loaded to 200 percent of the design load as specified. The soil nail head movement at each 
load increment up to the maximum test load was measured and recorded. Details of proof 
testing conducted on the selected soil nail anchors at the makai downslope of Site 1 are 
also presented in the attached Appendix. 
LIMITATIONS 
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities occurring 
simultaneously on a construction site; therefore, some of the work for the soil nail installation 
and testing may have occurred without our direct observation. 
Our services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards of 
geotechnical engineering practice; no warranty is expressed or implied. Provision of 
construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance, nor does it guarantee construction 
of any type.  The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of their work, for adhering 
to the plans and specifications, and for repairing defects regardless of when they are found.
